25:T776,<entryFree id="n21919" key="أَشَدُّ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أَشَدُّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [<hi rend="ital">Possessing the quality of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شِدَّة</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">in a greater,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">in the greatest, degree;</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">more,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">most, hard,</hi> &amp;c.]. See an ex. in a verse cited voce <foreign lang="ar">شِدَّةٌ</foreign>. <foreign lang="ar">حَلَبْتَ بِالسَّاعِدِ الأَشَدِّ</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar">حَلَبْتُهَا الخ</foreign>, is a prov., expl. in art. <foreign lang="ar">حلب</foreign>. And <foreign lang="ar">بَقِىَ أَشَدُّهُ</foreign>. [<hi rend="ital">The hardest part of it has remained</hi>] is another prov., applied to him who attains a part of that which he wants, and is unable to attain the completion thereof. (TA. [See also Freytag's “ Arab. Prov., ” i. 169.]) [With an indeterminate subst. or inf. n. following it in the accus. case, it supplies the place of a simple epithet denoting the comparative and superlative degrees; as in <foreign lang="ar">أَشَدُّ سَوَادًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">More,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">most, black;</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">أَشَدُّ غَضَبًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">More,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">most, angry.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَشَدُّ النَّهَارِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The time when the day is most advanced, the sun being at the highest.</hi> (L. [See <foreign lang="ar">شَدُّ النَّهَارِ</foreign>.])    </entryFree>26:T31b9,<entryFree id="n21907" key="شَدَّ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">شَدَّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, as an intrans. verb, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar" marker="$adi3a">شَدِدَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شِدَّةٌ</foreign>: see 8; and see also <foreign lang="ar">شِدَّةٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">لَشَدَّ مَا</foreign> is an expression used in the same sense as <foreign lang="ar">لَعَزَّ مَا</foreign> (A and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">عز</foreign>) and <foreign lang="ar">لَحَقَّ مَا</foreign>: (A and TA in that art.:) [and in like manner without the <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign>: thus] one says, <foreign lang="ar">شَدَّ مَا أَنَّكَ ذَاهِبٌ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">حَقَّ أَنَّكَ ذَاهِبٌ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">It is distressing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it distresses</hi> me, <hi rend="ital">that thou art going away</hi>]: and if you please, you may consider <foreign lang="ar">شَدَّ</foreign> as similar to <foreign lang="ar">نِعْمَ</foreign>; as when you say, <foreign lang="ar">نِعْمَ العَمَلُ أَنَّكَ تَقُولُ الحَقَّ</foreign> [Excellent, or most excellent, is the deed, thy saying the truth]. (Sb, TA.) [And it is also used to render intensive a verb following it; as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">لَشَدَّ مَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَبْغَضَنِى</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Much indeed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">greatly indeed, did he hate me.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شَدَّ عَلَيْهِ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar" marker="$ada3a">شَدَدَ</orth>
                  </form> (S, L) and      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar" marker="$adi3a">شَدِدَ</orth>
                  </form>, (L,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شَدٌّ</foreign> (S, L) and <foreign lang="ar">شُدُودٌ</foreign>, (L,) <hi rend="ital">He charged,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">made an assault</hi> or <hi rend="ital">attack, upon him,</hi> in war, or battle. (S, L.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">شَدَّ عَلَى العَدُوِّ شَدَّةً</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدَةً</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">شَدَّاتٍ كَثِيرَةً</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He made one charge,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">assault,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">attack, upon the enemy,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">many charges,</hi> &amp;c. (L.) And <foreign lang="ar">شَدَّ عَلَى قِرْنِهِ بِسِكِّينٍ</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar">بِعَصًا</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He made an assault,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">attack, upon his adversary, with a knife,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">with a staff;</hi> as also <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21907-1" target="اشتدّ" n="1" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n21912"/>عَلَيْهِ</foreign>. (Mgh.) And <foreign lang="ar">شَدَّ الذِّئْبُ عَلَى الغَنَمِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The wolf asaulted,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">attacked, the sheep</hi> or <hi rend="ital">goats.</hi> (L.) In the phrase, <foreign lang="ar">شَدُّوا الإِغَارَةَ</foreign>, the meaning is <foreign lang="ar">شَدُّوا لِلْإِغَارَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">They made a charge for the purpose of a sudden attack</hi> upon an enemy, or <hi rend="ital">a predatory incursion</hi>]; and therefore <foreign lang="ar">الاغارة</foreign> is put in the accus. case, not as an objective complement. (Ham p. 8.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شَدَّ</foreign>, (S,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="$adu3a">شَدُدَ</orth>
                  </form> and      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar" marker="$adi3a">شَدِدَ</orth>
                  </form>, (TK,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شَدٌّ</foreign>, (S, L, K,) also signifies <hi rend="ital">He ran;</hi> (S, L, * K; *) and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21907-2" target="اشتدّ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21912"/></foreign>. (S, L, K.) <foreign lang="ar">رُبَّ شَدٍّ فِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الكُرْزِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Many a run is in the sack</hi>] is a prov., originating from the fact that a man riding a pregnant mare was pursued by an enemy, and she cast her foal, which ran with its mother, whereupon the horseman alighted, and carried it off in a sack; and the enemy overtook him, and said to him, “Throw to me the foal;” and he replied in these words, meaning that the foal was of generous race: it is applied to him whose internal, or intrinsic, qualities are commended. (Meyd.) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">شَدَّ فِى العَدْوِ</foreign>, (A, Mgh, L,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شَدٌّ</foreign>; (L;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21907-3" target="اشتدّ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21912"/></foreign>; (A, Mgh, L;) <hi rend="ital">He hastened,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">was quick, in running:</hi> (Mgh, L:) and <foreign lang="ar">شَدَّ الإِحْضَارَ</foreign> [meaning the same]. (S in art. <foreign lang="ar">افر</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شَدَّ النَّهَارُ</foreign>, (S, L,) and <foreign lang="ar">الضُّحَى</foreign>, (L,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شَدٌّ</foreign>; (L, K; but in the latter, <foreign lang="ar">النَّار</foreign> is erroneously put for <foreign lang="ar">النَّهَار</foreign>; TA;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21907-4" target="اشتدّ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21912"/></foreign>; (L;) <hi rend="ital">The day,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">the morning, became advanced, the sun being high.</hi> (S, * L, K. *) [See also <foreign lang="ar">شَدٌّ</foreign> below.]       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شَدَّهُ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="$adu3a">شَدُدَ</orth>
                  </form> (S, A, L, Msb) and      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar" marker="$adi3a">شَدِدَ</orth>
                  </form>, the latter anomalous, for the aor. of a trans. verb of this class, of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعَلَ</foreign>, should be      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="$adu3a">شَدُدَ</orth>
                  </form> only, and that of an intrans. verb of the same class and measure should be      
    <form n="infl">

                  </form>, and this is the only instance, or almost the only one, of its kind, with both of these forms of aor., except <foreign lang="ar">عَلَّ</foreign> [and <foreign lang="ar">بَتَّ</foreign>] and <foreign lang="ar">نَمَّ</foreign>

                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Possessing the quality of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شِدَّة</foreign>: (S, L:) i. e. <hi rend="ital">hard;</hi> applied to a substance and to an attribute: <hi rend="ital">firm, compact,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sound:</hi> (L:) <hi rend="ital">strong, powerful, forceful; vigorous, robust, sturdy,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hardy;</hi> (A, Mgh, L, Msb;) applied to a thing, (Msb,) and to a man; (A, Mgh, L;) as also <foreign lang="ar">شَدِيدُ القُوَى</foreign>: (Mgh:) pl., applied to men, <foreign lang="ar">أَشِدَّآءُ</foreign> and [applied to things and men] <foreign lang="ar">شِدَادٌ</foreign> (A, L) and <foreign lang="ar">شُدُدٌ</foreign>, (Sb, L,) which last preserves its original form [without idghám] because not resembling a verb: (L:) also <hi rend="ital">courageous, brave, firm of heart:</hi> (L, K: *) and <hi rend="ital">niggardly, tenacious,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">avaricious;</hi> (A, L, Msb, K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21917-1" target="مُتَشَدِّدٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21923"/></foreign>: (S, A, L, K:) and [as is implied by the first explanation above, and shown by frequent usage,] <hi rend="ital">vehement, violent, intense, pressing, severe, strict, rigorous, tight, strait</hi> or <hi rend="ital">difficult, hard</hi> as meaning <hi rend="ital">hard to be borne, troublesome, distressing</hi> or <hi rend="ital">distressful, afflictive, calamitous,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">adverse.</hi> (L, KL, PS, &amp;c.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ شَدِيدٌ عَلَى قَوْمِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He is hard,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">severe,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rigorous, to his people</hi>]. (A.) [And <foreign lang="ar">شَدِيدٌ عَلَى كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Niggardly, tenacious,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">avaricious, of such a thing.</hi>] Aboo-Dhu-eyb says, using <foreign lang="ar">شَدِيد</foreign> in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">شَحِيح</foreign>, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">حَدَرْنَاهُ بِالأَثْوَابِ فِى قَعْرِ هُوَّةٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">شَدِيدٍ عَلَى مَا ضُمَّ فِى اللَّحْدِ جُولُهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">We lowered him, with the</hi> grave-<hi rend="ital">clothes, into the bottom of a cavity in the ground, the sides whereof were tenacious of what was comprised in the lateral hollow which was the place of the corpse</hi>]. (L.) And the words of the Kur [c. 8], <foreign lang="ar">وَإِنَّهُ لِحُبِّ الخَيْرِ لَشَدِيدٌ</foreign>, accord. to Zj, mean <hi rend="ital">And verily, on account of the love of wealth, he is niggardly,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tenacious,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">avaricious.</hi> (L.) <foreign lang="ar">شَدِيدُ العَيْنِ</foreign> applied to a man, and <foreign lang="ar">شَدِيْدَةُ جَفْنِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">العَيْنِ</foreign> metaphorically applied by a poet to a she-camel, mean <hi rend="ital">Whom sleep does not overcome.</hi> (L.) And <foreign lang="ar">الشَّدِيدُ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">The lion;</hi> (K;) because of his strength and hardiness. (TA.) [<foreign lang="ar">شَدِيد</foreign> with a subst. or an inf. n. following it in the gen. case, the latter having the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign> prefixed to it, or being prefixed to another noun in the gen. case, supplies the place of an intensive epithet; as in <foreign lang="ar">شَدِيدُ السَّوَادِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Intensely,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">very, black;</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">شَدِيدُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الغَضَبِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Vehemently,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">exceedingly,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">very, angry;</hi> and] <foreign lang="ar">مِسْكٌ شَدِيدُ الرَّائِحَةِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Strong-smelling musk;</hi> (L;) [and <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ شَدِيدُ بَيَاضِ العَيْنِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A man intensely white in the eye.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الحُرُوفُ الشَّدِيدَةُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The strong letters</hi>] are <hi rend="ital">those letters which, in a state of quiescence, prevent the current of the voice in their utterance;</hi> namely <foreign lang="ar">أ</foreign>, <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign>, <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign>, <foreign lang="ar">ج</foreign>, <foreign lang="ar">د</foreign>, <foreign lang="ar">ط</foreign>, <foreign lang="ar">ق</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">and</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ك</foreign>; (TA;) <hi rend="ital">the letters comprised in the words</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَجَدْتَ طَبَقَكَ</foreign>. (K.)    </entryFree>2e:Tfe8,<entryFree id="n21920" key="أَشُدٌّ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أَشُدٌّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, A, Mgh, L, K, &amp;c.,) also pronounced <foreign lang="ar">أُشُدٌّ</foreign>, (Seer, K,) but the latter form is rare, (TA,) is both masc. and fem., (Zj, TA,) and as used in the Kur it has somewhat different meanings: (Az, TA:) in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ أَشُدَّهُ</foreign>, (S, K,) and other phrases in the Kur, (TA,) <foreign lang="ar">أَشُدّ</foreign> is expl. as meaning The <hi rend="ital">state of strength;</hi> (S, Mgh, L, K;) which is <hi rend="ital">from eighteen to thirty years:</hi> (S, L, K:) or <hi rend="ital">from about seventeen to forty:</hi> (Zj:) or <hi rend="ital">from thirty to forty:</hi> (Zj in another place:) or <hi rend="ital">puberty:</hi> (Az, Mgh, L:) or <hi rend="ital">firmness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">soundness, of judgment, produced by experience:</hi> (L:) or <hi rend="ital">puberty together with such maturity as gives evidence of rectitude of conduct</hi> or <hi rend="ital">course of life;</hi> (Zj, Az, Mgh, L;) <hi rend="ital">which may be at,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">before, the age of eighteen years;</hi> accord. to most of the men of science, and among them Esh-Sháfi'ee; (Zj, Az, L;) <hi rend="ital">and the extreme term of which is three and thirty years:</hi> (Mgh:) or the <hi rend="ital">age of forty years;</hi> as in the Kur xlvi. 14: (L:) <foreign lang="ar">أَشُدٌّ</foreign> [originally <foreign lang="ar">أَشْدُدٌ</foreign>] is a sing. having a pl. form, like <foreign lang="ar">آنُكٌ</foreign>; and these two words are [said to be] the only instances of the kind: (S, K: [but see <foreign lang="ar">آنُكٌ</foreign>:]) or a pl. having no proper sing., (S, Mgh, K,) like <foreign lang="ar">آسَالٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَبَابِيلُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَبَادِيدُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَذَاكِيرُ</foreign>: (S:) or its sing. is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21920-1" target="شِدَّةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21915"/></foreign>, (AHeyth, S, Mgh, K,) accord. to Sb; and this is good with respect to the meaning, because one says, <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ الغُلَامُ شِدَّتَهُ</foreign>; (S;) but <foreign lang="ar">فِعْلَةٌ</foreign> does not form a pl. of the measure <foreign lang="ar">أَفْعُلٌ</foreign>; (S, K;) for as to <foreign lang="ar">أَنْعُمٌ</foreign>, (S,) which is said by AHeyth to be pl. of <foreign lang="ar">نِعْمَةٌ</foreign>, (TA,) [and respecting which Mtr says that] <foreign lang="ar">أَشُدٌّ</foreign> is said to be pl. of <foreign lang="ar">شِدَّةٌ</foreign> like as <foreign lang="ar">أَنْعُمٌ</foreign> is of <foreign lang="ar">نِعْمَةٌ</foreign>, formed by regarding the <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> as elided, (Mgh, [and AHeyth says the like,]) it is only pl. of <foreign lang="ar">نُعْمٌ</foreign> in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمُ نُعْمٍ</foreign>: (S:) or its sing. is <foreign lang="ar">شَدٌّ</foreign>, like as <foreign lang="ar">كَلْبٌ</foreign> is of <foreign lang="ar">أَكْلُبٌ</foreign>; or <foreign lang="ar">شِدٌّ</foreign>, like as <foreign lang="ar">ذِئْبٌ</foreign> is of <foreign lang="ar">أَذْؤُبٌ</foreign>; (S, K;) accord. to some; (S;) but neither <foreign lang="ar">شَدٌّ</foreign> nor <foreign lang="ar">شِدٌّ</foreign> has been heard from the Arabs [as sing. of <foreign lang="ar">أَشُدٌّ</foreign>]; and they are only deduced from analogy: (S, K:) or it is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أَشَدُّ</foreign>; and the <foreign lang="ar">أ</foreign> is not regarded in the formation of this pl.
